<div id="review_2625887033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2625887033" />
    <a title="YUFANGYUAN LIU" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87868373-yufangyuan-liu"><img alt="YUFANGYUAN LIU" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2625887033?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YUFANGYUAN LIU" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YUFANGYUAN LIU" href="/user/show/87868373-yufangyuan-liu">YUFANGYUAN LIU</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2625887033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3878757837146489498">While most of the students are likely to read comic or fictional books, I personally prefer historical novel to any other genres. I recently read the novel—Romance of The Three Kingdoms by Luo Guanzhong—that was written in the fourteenth century. Being one of the most famous novels for ancient Chinese history, It is definitely worthy for students to spend their leisure time on reading Romance of the Three Kingdoms.<br/><br/>To begin with, In Romance of The Three Kingdoms, lords and generals from kingdoms </span>
  <span id="freeText3878757837146489498" style="display:none">While most of the students are likely to read comic or fictional books, I personally prefer historical novel to any other genres. I recently read the novel—Romance of The Three Kingdoms by Luo Guanzhong—that was written in the fourteenth century. Being one of the most famous novels for ancient Chinese history, It is definitely worthy for students to spend their leisure time on reading Romance of the Three Kingdoms.<br /><br />To begin with, In Romance of The Three Kingdoms, lords and generals from kingdoms fight for supremacy. Three great leaders emerge in the beginning, including Liu Bei, Cao Cao, and Sun Quan. These are men of formidable character, prowess, and guile, each keen to see his ambition fulfilled. They are rulers of their own kingdoms and their desire is to unite the three kingdoms, bringing together “All Under Heaven,” as they call it. Specifically, there are numerous dramatic stories that depict unforgettable details for how each leader successfully win significant battles or unfortunately defeats. Also, the author summarizes up numbers of brilliant military strategies for both defense and offense that are used by generals. Personally, I believe that author’s text adequately reach the intended audience who are interested in history, military, or war strategies. However, since this book was translated from another language and written in long time ago, it might be challenging for students to completely understand every single details. Readers may feel lost due to some new vocabulary, but the brilliant plots and vivid stories can surely keep motivating them to read on. <br /><br />The author definitely considered the geographic in ancient China to conceive the ideal position for three kingdoms and the locations of important battlefields. More importantly, since the period of the three kingdoms occurred in the early third century, the author needed collect pieces of evidence from folks that possibly have heard about some myths and stories that happened in the early period. I agree with the author about the final result of the three kingdom. In the end, Liu Bei, one of the most powerful general overcomes numbers of obstacles and eventually united three kingdoms. I believe Liu Bei should be the appropriate ruler among all the lords and generals because he is the only one who promotes virtuous leadership. Liu Bei has a heart to peacefully embrace the world, and he wants to utilize his kindness instead of cruelty to rule the kingdoms.<br /><br />Last but not least, I particularly enjoy reading this book because the author illustrates detailed images for the fighting scenes perfectly and concludes the significance of the utilization of war strategies for every battle. It worked well for me due to the fact that I am interested in history and military, and learning ancient Chinese history can unquestionably raise my cultural awareness. When I compare this book with the The Art of War by Sun T, I can clearly see the advantages. Although the genre of them are both historical, the Romance of The Three Kingdoms covers much more topics, such as people’ inner feelings, relationships, and alliances. In The Art of War, however, It simply clarifies military strategies without introducing interesting storylines and mentioning any characters’ emotions. <br /><br />Romance of The Three Kingdoms appeals greatly to me in an emotional way in the chapter of Formation of Brotherhood. One of the most memorable quote is “We three though of different families, swear brotherhood, and promise mutual help to one end. We will rescue each other in difficulty; we will aid each other in danger. We swear to serve the state and save the people.We ask not the same day of birth, but we seek to die together.” When three generals from the same Kingdom make vows for their friendships, I personally become emotional because of my admiration for their everlasting friendship. Last but not least, I would undoubtedly recommend this book to my friends or anyone who has interests on military subjects, battle strategies, or history.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3878757837146489498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2513231844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2513231844" />
    <a title="Silvio Curtis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852180-silvio-curtis"><img alt="Silvio Curtis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416076272p2/1852180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2513231844?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvio Curtis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvio Curtis" href="/user/show/1852180-silvio-curtis">Silvio Curtis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2513231844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8775400131448081639">This is one of the first Chinese novels, and long enough that this translation is split into two parts. It's a partly fictionalized version, written a millennium after the fact, of the end of the Han dynasty. It blames the beginning of the chaos on corrupt eunuchs who everyone else hated. The eunuchs themselves are soon massacred, but their killers have their own designs on supreme power, and the situation descends into a civil war with many sides, whose number and identity are constantly shifti</span>
  <span id="freeText8775400131448081639" style="display:none">This is one of the first Chinese novels, and long enough that this translation is split into two parts. It's a partly fictionalized version, written a millennium after the fact, of the end of the Han dynasty. It blames the beginning of the chaos on corrupt eunuchs who everyone else hated. The eunuchs themselves are soon massacred, but their killers have their own designs on supreme power, and the situation descends into a civil war with many sides, whose number and identity are constantly shifting as warlords and ministers double- and triple-cross each other, snatching the emperor from each other like the ball in an American football match. This is different from epic poems by always keeping the focus on the clever strategists and not on the fighters. They're so devious I kept chuckling out loud on the bus! The book does suspense better than any other work of ancient literature I've encountered - in one conversation between two major characters, one of whom is planning betrayal and the other of whom may or may not suspect it, a sudden clap of thunder almost made me jump as much as the traitor did. I also was surprised at how close to amorality the narrative persona is. Although it focuses on two sides more than any others - one led by the schemer Cao Cao, and one by Liu Bei, a distant relative of the emperor, with his sworn "brothers" - it would be a real stretch to call them evil and good. Liu Bei certainly has more principles, but he doesn't get anywhere until he picks up some ministers who can talk him out of following them. Since this is an early twentieth century translation, it doesn't use the jarringly modern language that most translations of old literature do now, but I wish it had an index and possibly a map, because I was constantly losing track of who was who and who was winning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8775400131448081639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2571324023" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2571324023" />
    <a title="Mary Soon Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6731291-mary-soon-lee"><img alt="Mary Soon Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438179396p2/6731291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2571324023?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Soon Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Soon Lee" href="/user/show/6731291-mary-soon-lee">Mary Soon Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6731291-mary-soon-lee?shelf=chinese-classics">chinese-classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2571324023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8913483851781238512">This is the first half of C. H. Brewitt-Taylor's translation of the 14th-century Chinese classic. I am reading his translation in parallel with Moss Roberts's translation: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/158770.Three_Kingdoms_Classic_Novel_in_Four_Volumes' title='Three Kingdoms Classic Novel in Four Volumes by Luo Guanzhong' rel='nofollow noopener'>Three Kingdoms: Classic Novel in Four Volumes</a>. While I am unable to judge the comparative accuracy of the two renditions, as a reader I considerably prefer Roberts's translation, primarily due to his extensive and illuminating endnotes. Lacking the information in those endnotes, I think I would have been unable to appreciate t</span>
  <span id="freeText8913483851781238512" style="display:none">This is the first half of C. H. Brewitt-Taylor's translation of the 14th-century Chinese classic. I am reading his translation in parallel with Moss Roberts's translation: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/158770.Three_Kingdoms_Classic_Novel_in_Four_Volumes" title="Three Kingdoms Classic Novel in Four Volumes by Luo Guanzhong" rel="nofollow noopener">Three Kingdoms: Classic Novel in Four Volumes</a>. While I am unable to judge the comparative accuracy of the two renditions, as a reader I considerably prefer Roberts's translation, primarily due to his extensive and illuminating endnotes. Lacking the information in those endnotes, I think I would have been unable to appreciate the narrative.<br /><br />There are two respects in which I do prefer the Brewitt-Taylor translation. Firstly, he inserts paragraph breaks when the text switches from one speaker to another, which aids clarity. Secondly, I mostly prefer his renditions of the poetry. He also adopts a somewhat more archaic prose style than Roberts does, which may appeal to some readers (though not me) as suggesting the story's venerable age. The original Chinese novel was penned over six hundred years ago, and is based on historical events from about 200 A.D.<br /><br />I note that I am finding it helpful to read each chapter twice, once in each translation. The book has a vast cast of characters, none of whom I was familiar with before, but many of whom would have been known to its original audience. Reading a chapter again allows me a sense of what it would be like if I wasn't trying to remember who everybody was and which faction they supported. (Although this is slightly undermined by the two translations using different schemes for transliterating Chinese names.)<br /><br />I will postpone comment on the book's quality as a story until I eventually make my way to the end.<br /><br />P.S. My rating of 3 out of 5 stars is as much a rating for the translation as for the underlying story, and I may well end up giving the Roberts's translation a higher rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8913483851781238512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

One moment I read about a villager who served his own wife as being wolf meat to a warrior. The warrior found out when he had accidently seen the remains in the kitchen. However, instead of being the least shocked (which I would certainly be) the warrior praised the villager for his loyalty!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10055413748382119214">The problems with this story are the exact problems you'd expect if you know anything about the Romance of the Three Kingdoms. One of the first things anyone would learn about the story is that it's very long and has way too many characters. It is very long and there way too many characters, but as it went along my mind, as other reviews have said, did start to focus solely on the handful of important characters.   <span id="freeText10055413748382119214" style="display:none">The problems with this story are the exact problems you'd expect if you know anything about the Romance of the Three Kingdoms. One of the first things anyone would learn about the story is that it's very long and has way too many characters. It is very long and there way too many characters, but as it went along my mind, as other reviews have said, did start to focus solely on the handful of important characters. This story doesn't have the scenes of character growth or have anything that could really be called a character arc, but it's a story written hundreds of years ago so most of the flaws should be excused at least in some way. Despite all of that, the story can get quite tedious, but I would say it is worth the read to see some the strange moral choices that apparently must have seemed just fine 500 years ago.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2792577915805740231">Which was longer, this or the three volumes of "1,001 Arabian Nights"? You're probably thinking "Nights", but did I mention there's another volume of "Three Kingdoms "? More importantly, which seemed longer? This is, I think, largely a matter of the taste of the reader. Ergo, "De gustibus non est disputandum!" In my opinion, "Nights" provided more diversity of storylines and was, therefore, more interesting, more enjoyable.   <span id="freeText2792577915805740231" style="display:none">Which was longer, this or the three volumes of "1,001 Arabian Nights"? You're probably thinking "Nights", but did I mention there's another volume of "Three Kingdoms "? More importantly, which seemed longer? This is, I think, largely a matter of the taste of the reader. Ergo, "De gustibus non est disputandum!" In my opinion, "Nights" provided more diversity of storylines and was, therefore, more interesting, more enjoyable. I was, however, delighted to see a mention of a previous read; "Records of the Grand Historian" by Ssuma Chien. He was killed for not writing history in a way that was more complementary to the existing powers.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lldtV+CM5uXvyvoqTrUgvgn/4Ls5rpRXUH+YGRqe1po1NwIu3zu6P5AFpadguJrpKEEhiKxYjzBmSCK2U7Wc7Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m6hO3BvOw4xWaAf7M/7ryLeut/fw7w0MulXHtK8ybYo4yCGlJHmfVimnWHYd81GflhB2xGUZFmuMYn0b5hkn/Q==')})
  }

Besides being a former slave, he was lame in one leg and walked with a crutch. After a decade of teaching in Rome, he was banished by Emperor Domitian; undaunted, he established a school in Greece.  The Manual is a collection of Epictetus\' essential teachings and pithy sayings, compiled by his closet student. It is the most accessible and actionable guide to Stoic philosophy, as relevant today as it was in the Roman Empire.This new edition is rendered in contemporary English, with a foreword, by Sam Torode. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7502722276177420266"><b>Luo Ben</b> (c. 1330–1400), better known by his style name <b>Luo Guanzhong</b> (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13733431.___' title='罗贯中' rel='nofollow noopener'>罗贯中</a>) (Mandarin pronunciation: [lwɔ kwantʂʊŋ]), was a Chinese writer who lived during the Yuan Dynasty. He was also known by his pseudonym <i>Huhai Sanren</i> (Chinese: 湖海散人; pinyin: Húhǎi Sǎnrén; literally "Leisure Man of Lakes and Seas"). Luo was attributed with writing <i>Romance of the Three Kingdoms</i> and editing <i>Water Margin</i>, two of th</span>
  <span id="freeText7502722276177420266" style="display:none"><b>Luo Ben</b> (c. 1330–1400), better known by his style name <b>Luo Guanzhong</b> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13733431.___" title="罗贯中" rel="nofollow noopener">罗贯中</a>) (Mandarin pronunciation: [lwɔ kwantʂʊŋ]), was a Chinese writer who lived during the Yuan Dynasty. He was also known by his pseudonym <i>Huhai Sanren</i> (Chinese: 湖海散人; pinyin: Húhǎi Sǎnrén; literally "Leisure Man of Lakes and Seas"). Luo was attributed with writing <i>Romance of the Three Kingdoms</i> and editing <i>Water Margin</i>, two of the Four Great Classical Novels of Chinese literature.</span>

Liu Pei, the legitimate heir to the Han throne, elects to fight for his birthright and enlists the aid of his sworn brothers, the impulsive giant Chang Fei and the invincible knight Kuan Yu. The brave band faces a formidable array of enemies, foremost among them the treacherous and bloodthirsty Ts\'ao Ts\'ao. The bold struggle of the three heroes seems doomed until the reclusive wizard Chuko Liang offers his counsel, and the tide begins to turn.\n\nRomance of the Three Kingdoms is China\'s oldest novel and the first of a great tradition of historical fiction. Believed to have been compiled by the play-wright Lo Kuan-chung in the late fourteenth century, it is indebted to the great San-kuo chi (Chronicles of the Three Kingdoms) completed by the historian Ch\'en Shou just before his death in 297 CE. The novel first appeared in print in 1522. This edition, translated in the mid-1920s by C. H. Brewitt-Taylor, is based on a shortened and simplified version which appeared in the 1670s. An Introduction to this reprint by Robert E. Hegel, Professor of Chinese and Comparative Literature at Washington University, provides an insightful commentary on the historical background to the novel, its literary origins and its main
